    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2027531689" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2027531689" />
    <a title="Michael Joosten" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16190400-michael-joosten"><img alt="Michael Joosten" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1357571827p2/16190400.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2027531689?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael Joosten" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael Joosten" href="/user/show/16190400-michael-joosten">Michael Joosten</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780553578737" href="/book/show/775494.I_Jedi">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2027531689" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14313317141006689188">My review here should be taken with a grain of salt, because rereading <i>I, Jedi</i> now is as much about digging up old Star Wars memories (from when there were no more than one, maybe two prequels) as it is about the book itself. Reading some of the other reviews here, I see critiques that make sense to me. This may not be a perfect book...<br/><br/>...but I still like it, by and large. <br/><br/>I like Corran Horn, though. If you DON'T like him, you're dead in the water here, because Corran isn't just the protagonist,</span>
  <span id="freeText14313317141006689188" style="display:none">My review here should be taken with a grain of salt, because rereading <i>I, Jedi</i> now is as much about digging up old Star Wars memories (from when there were no more than one, maybe two prequels) as it is about the book itself. Reading some of the other reviews here, I see critiques that make sense to me. This may not be a perfect book...<br /><br />...but I still like it, by and large. <br /><br />I like Corran Horn, though. If you DON'T like him, you're dead in the water here, because Corran isn't just the protagonist, isn't just the only character the story follows--he's the one speaking in the first person. <br /><br />I also don't mind that Stackpole spends a third of the book rewriting the background of the Jedi Academy trilogy so that Corran is a.) present and b.) a major actor. I don't mind this for two reasons: 1.) I never really *liked* the Jedi Academy trilogy (I share Corran's antipathy toward Kyp Durron, especially) and 2.) the entire Expanded Universe is one long attempt to insert things into the background of the movies and impress upon you that they had an effect upon it. Doing this to another EU book just furthers that tradition. To my mind, it's part of the fun.<br /><br />Stackpole's writing here is far more Rogue Squadron than it is Jedi Academy--even when he's writing about Jedi and the Force. Not everything holds up post-prequels, let alone post-Disney, but the overall fit isn't terrible. Corran's analytical combat side reminded me quite a bit of Batman (ironically, given Batman's reputation as the most prominent non-superpowered superhero). I suspect that Stackpole would have got a lot of mileage out of midichlorians.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14313317141006689188" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText6475254249786361685" style="display:none">I both loved and hated this book. I loved the characters and everything about this story, but I absolutely despised the motive. This book features Corran Horn of Rogue Squadron and the early part of the book really ties in with the Jedi Academy trilogy. I had no idea that in that trilogy the apprentice Keiran Halcyon was actually Horn undercover. I probably loved that idea too much! It made for a very entertaining read. <br /><br />What I didn't like about the book was that a) Corran's wife was kidnapped and put in stasis for months and months until a rescue was attempted. But no, three weeks is fine. Anyway, when I could ignore that part, I found it to be an excellent novel.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12924608076177696256">This is definitely my favorite out of the four Star Wars novels I have read. I had read the Thrawn Triology by Timothy Zahn and even though the storyline was good, I didn't like the writing. That was the case with this book. I really liked how the story was told in first person because it really made Corran more realistic. I really liked Corran as a character and am going to look into more books with him in it. I actually liked him better than Luke Skywalker.<br/><br/>I really enjoyed this book and when I</span>
  <span id="freeText12924608076177696256" style="display:none">This is definitely my favorite out of the four Star Wars novels I have read. I had read the Thrawn Triology by Timothy Zahn and even though the storyline was good, I didn't like the writing. That was the case with this book. I really liked how the story was told in first person because it really made Corran more realistic. I really liked Corran as a character and am going to look into more books with him in it. I actually liked him better than Luke Skywalker.<br /><br />I really enjoyed this book and when I took time to read it, it was hard for me to put down. The only thing I didn't really like is that it left some things unexplained. I don't want to say what because of spoilers but it has something to do with Exar Kun. Also, sometimes the dialogue was a little cheesy but that's to be expected in a Star Wars book, lol. Overall, I thought this was a good book and would recommend it to any Star Wars fans. However, I wouldn't let kids under 12 read it because there is quite a bit mentioned about sex. There's no actual sex scenes, but it's talk about. Other than that little warning for parents, I thought this was an awesome book!</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2917438296" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2917438296" />
    <a title="Suden" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68100915-suden"><img alt="Suden" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518982454p2/68100915.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2917438296?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Suden" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Suden" href="/user/show/68100915-suden">Suden</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780553578737" href="/book/show/775494.I_Jedi">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68100915-suden?shelf=rated-5-awesome-worth-reading-again">rated-5-awesome-worth-reading-again</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2917438296" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10822340092800433384">"The Sue is strong with this one." (But luckily, that's not the only thing I have to say about this work.)<br/><br/>Yes -- the Gary Stu effect is the one thing that really bothered me, here. It plagues the book. If not for the large chunks of internal dialogue and soul-searching (which were well-enough executed to mitigate the annoyance), I might really have hated Corran Horn for it. He is too perfect in his actions and decisions; but at least he is more-often-than-not insecure about it all -- and that ma</span>
  <span id="freeText10822340092800433384" style="display:none">"The Sue is strong with this one." (But luckily, that's not the only thing I have to say about this work.)<br /><br />Yes -- the Gary Stu effect is the one thing that really bothered me, here. It plagues the book. If not for the large chunks of internal dialogue and soul-searching (which were well-enough executed to mitigate the annoyance), I might really have hated Corran Horn for it. He is too perfect in his actions and decisions; but at least he is more-often-than-not insecure about it all -- and that makes him a bit more human...ish.<br /><br />What I did hate, is the way in which he at times seems to be the better of Luke Skywalker. (Yes! That Luke; the full-blown Jedi main character who is the central hero of the original franchise's tail end!) It's not that Horn is that good -- no, it's that Skywalker is purposefully made to seem just that bit more incompetent, ignorant or unimaginative, and overly insecure. Well... the insecure part I could get over with -- it's logical, and human, for a teacher in Luke's position. But the overall sentiment is that Horn is just shown off to be too competent and too powerful next to Luke... not on his own merits, but at Luke's expense. And I'm not even a Luke fan (at all) -- I just like good writing and good (fan) fiction integration. And I feel Luke's prominence and importance -- which he won over many obstacles, a hefty history and background, and in many installments -- was not done justice here. I felt it to be a bit... disrespectful.<br /><br />Aside from that major downside, however, I actually think that said integration is very well done. And aside from my irritation at how Luke's competence was handled by the writer, I enjoyed this novel in a way I hadn't any other, in a long time (Ready Player One was a better novel and even more awesome, but perhaps because of that, it wasn't as relaxing a ride). It was solid 5* material for the most part. And while typing this, I'm still not sure whether to subtract a * for my beef with the fan fiction feel that Gary Horn... Ah, Corran Stu... well, the main character... provided me with.<br /><br />Of the Jedi Academy trilogy, I only read pt.1 ("Jedi Search") when it had just been published. So, that's around a quarter century ago. I loved it even more than the Thrawn trilogy -- it felt even more like Wars to me -- but when my interests were drawn into metal music, and the Trek side of sci-fi (and I also couldn't get ahold of a borrowed copy and wanted to buy CDs instead), I somehow neglected to read the other parts. Which I always regretted -- especially when I later fell head over heels for the Tales Of The Jedi and KOTOR stories, which are related to The Big Evil in these books. Some years ago, I intended to make up for my omission -- I have borrowed "Apprentice" and "Champions" from my pal, Reese. Outstanding!<br /><br />But it took me a while to get back into Wars full-time, or at least to the point where I could stomach a novel. To get into the flow of the Academy story again, I decided to first read this-here companion work -- "I Jedi". And that was a good choice; it made me remember a number of important things about "Jedi Search". (I chose not to re-read that first part -- I read too slowly, and I want to read so many other books, that it'd defeat the purpose. And there's Wookieepedia, at that.)<br /><br />Fun detail -- I knew nothing yet about the Camaasi, but I've already seen that I'm about to read (and see) about them in the comic omnibus (Knights Of The Old Rep) that I've also been reading. So it was nice to read about them here, too.<br /><br />Conversely, I'd already read about that other Big Evil -- or little, since she's short of stature -- in the X-Wing comics. I hardly remembered Tavira, but it mostly came back to me, and I love my nostalgic strolls down memory canyon.<br /><br />I've come across 1 or 2 reviews that lament the fact that Horn (hmm, ill-chosen part of his name, for this argument?) actually -- oh, my! -- considers playing out the seduction game with Tavira in practice, for the good of his mission... of finding his wife. Well, yes, it's not the most honourable thing to do -- but, I'm sorry ladies -- come on! He's a secret agent. It's a book for adults, not for children; it needn't be censored. Of course he would consider it. She's described as beautiful -- most men (if not all) would. And actual, real-life, professional female covert operatives would, too, I'm sure. ("Homeland", anybody?) Yes, men have "that" side -- it's in their biology. Not nice, not fair, not pretty -- but science and fact. And often, they do choose to ignore that side of their feelings in favour of their chosen spouse. But any male who says he never looks at -- or thinks about sleeping with -- other women, is... well, perhaps not lying outright, but... suspect. I feel it's better to be honest about humanity's primal drives (women have theirs, too -- albeit a bit less "selfish"-feeling), and confront them from the perspective of knowledge, than to try and shove them under the rug. I feel the latter's bound to bring more problems in the end; actual faithlessness may eventually ensue if a person does not confront their true feelings about the subject.<br />And I'm afraid that any female who ignores these general truths, is deluding herself.<br />Oh, and in the end -- I won't spoil Horn's choices, but I think there's ultimately a lot of mitigating circumstances going for him. So... I see not much of a problem. I'd love him all the more for the whole of it, had I been his wife.<br /><br />(TLDR: I'm not condoning adultery. I am condoning it for the good of saving a life or, possibly, for accomplishing a mission. I do see where it may come from -- basic instinct -- and I think it's better to talk about that openly, instead of ignoring the fact that men's drive to procreate works differently from women's. I believe that's in a couple's best interest. Wait -- this was "TL" in it's own right, too.)<br /><br />What I loved to read about was the actual making of Corran's light saber -- although, in all honesty, I might have done it totally differently myself and didn't much care for the actual content / ideas that were presented. But I have been living with Wars, on-and-off, for 3 decades; I have made 3 sabers myself (one of carton when I was 10YO, one of LEGO at age 16, and a rugged-but-beautiful custom one constructed mostly of metal -- it weighs nigh a kg -- when I was 22) and have written about these interesting weapons in my own fan fiction. So I had high expectations, and was a bit disappointed at how it was handled in this novel. Yet if that's the way it "actually" goes (or went, in the Wars Legends), then I must accept those facts. And, aside from all that, it was a very nice treat and surprise that light saber construction was dealt with in such technical and metaphysical detail, and length, in this novel! So, result-wise, it felt like a win.<br /><br />On a tangient... Rather; on a side "note", this novel -- and any subsequent ones -- were a great excuse to re-explore my love for John Williams' (and others') musical scores for the franchise. I loved them as a kid, but had grown more fond of other composers over the years; but returning to them now, while reading this book, was much fun. I think I just might've listened to them too much, because I still -- or again? -- love the soundtracks to the original trilogy. And I'm growing to like the newer stuff, too.<br /><br />The pace was slow indeed -- as some reviewers have mentioned -- but to me, actually, that was a big plus. I don't read books just to experience frantic dogfights and sabre action (although I expect and appreciate some of those elements), but I also want to know about the motivations, thoughts and feelings of the characters, the backgrounds of the plot, and descriptions of the hardware and surroundings. This novel had plenty of all that.<br /><br />The epilogue featured a powerful proverb (not Stackpole's own wisdom, but quoted in appropriate Wars jargon), reminding me of what I need to keep in mind dealing with my own life:<br />âWhen the only tool that you have is a hydrospanner, every problem looks like something that needs to be torqued.â<br />(Yes, I added it to the quotes pool. No, it didn't exist before -- I looked. But I did neglect to add the book title, and can't edit it; hence it only shows up under the author's name.) A rather unexpected moment, for a pulp / genre novel like this.<br /><br />And even Pellaeon was mentioned -- my favourite 'ImpStar Deuce' captain after Lennox. Yep, that does it -- for all its flaws, and if only for diversity, this one does get all 5 of 'em.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10822340092800433384" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/513207.Champions_of_the_Force"><img alt="Champions of the Force (Star Wars: The Jedi Academy Trilogy, #3)" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1327008722l/513207._SY160_.jpg" />
</a>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('LF9iA7LZSNOLXjChpCr0IIOI5HxLJRPlcXn707aLQLei2in1yOB3v1dtgF6+k3XYYvznVO+vZ2RB3z8esPf3cw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
